Eileen Fulton, Longtime ‘Bad Girl' Lisa on ‘As the World Turns,' Dies at 91
Source: The Hollywood Reporter    Published: 2025-07-20 06:56:15

Subscribe for full access to The Hollywood Reporter Subscribe for full access to The Hollywood Reporter She spent nearly 50 years on the CBS soap opera, and her conniving character went through eight husbands. By Mike Barnes Senior Editor Eileen Fulton, the minister's daughter who spent the better part of 50 years portraying Lisa Miller, one of the first “bad girls” of daytime television, on the CBS soap opera As the World Turns, has died. She was 91. Fulton died Monday in Asheville, North Carolina, after “a period of declining health,” her family announced. Four years into the run of As the World Turns, Fulton joined the No. 1 daytime drama in 1960 for what was originally supposed to be a three-month summer storyline. She exited the soap three times — once to headline her own primetime spinoff, 1965's Our Private World — but continued on through the final episode broadcast Sept. 17, 2010. Related Stories News Alan Bergman, Oscar-Winning Lyricist, Dies at 99 Movies Kate Beckinsale Announces Death of Her Mother, British Actress Judy Loe, at 78: "I Am Paralyzed" Her Lisa had eight husbands, with Nicolas Coster portraying two of them. Three of her marriages ended in divorce, four ended in death and one was annulled. When As the World Turns was done, her character's full name was Lisa Miller Hughes Eldridge Shea Colman McColl Mitchell Grimaldi Chedwyn. She also had lots and lots of lovers. “She's a romantic, that's why she falls in love so much,” Fulton said in a 2005 conversation for the Television Academy Foundation website The Interviews. Inducted into the Soap Opera Hall of Fame in 1998 and given a lifetime achievement award from the Daytime Emmys in 2004, Fulton was one of the first soap actors to have her own publicist. She also employed a bodyguard to protect her from angry viewers who disapproved of what Lisa was up to. “They had a great love/hate thing [with me], it was amazing,” she said. And in the '70s, Fulton famously had a clause inserted into her contract that guaranteed she would never have to play a grandmother. “At that time, grandmothers had no romance at all — and I wasn't about to let that happen to me,” she told the Los Angeles Times in 2000. She eventually became OK with that. The oldest of three kids, Margaret Elizabeth McLarty was born in Asheville on Sept. 13, 1933. Her mother, Peggy, was a schoolteacher and her father, James, a Methodist preacher. She said she knew by the third grade that she was going to be an actress. After graduating from Lee Edwards High School in her hometown and, in 1956, as a music and drama major from Greensboro College, she moved to New York and studied acting with Sanford Meisner at the Neighborhood Playhouse, where one of her classmates was Keir Dullea. Fulton had played a hooker in Girl of the Night (1960), starring Anne Francis, when someone from As the World Turns called her manager looking to see if one of his clients, East of Eden actress Lois Smith, was available to play Lisa. Smith was not, so he suggested Fulton. “I knew I was going to get that part. There were 250 other girls there [at the audition], but I just knew,” she said. Lisa “was supposed to be the sweet girl next door. I said, ‘I'm tired of being the sweet girl next door.' I can't change the lines, but I can change my intention once we're on the air. I just thought of little conniving things I could do to Bob.” That would be her first TV husband, played by Don Hastings. During one stretch in the early '60s, Fulton would work in the mornings on As the World Turns (when it aired lived), race to the Billy Rose Theater on Broadway to play Honey in matinee performances of Who's Afraid of Virginia Woolf? and then appear downtown at the Sullivan Street Playhouse in the evenings in The Fantasticks. Fulton quit As the World Turns for the first time in 1963 to “do other things,” which included an off-Broadway turn opposite Hal Holbrook in Abe Lincoln in Illinois. As she had trouble finding other work, viewers did not take to her replacement, Pamela King, and so she returned. She left again in 1965, this time to star in Our Private World, which aired Wednesday and Friday nights on CBS. Lisa had fled Oakdale after dumping Bob to move to Chicago, where she wed the wealthy John Eldridge. (Coster played Eldridge; decades later, he would portray Lisa's seventh husband, Eduardo Grimaldi.) Our Private World, however, was canceled in September after just four months on the air, and Fulton was back on As the World Turns in 1966. In 1983, Fulton exited in a contract dispute, to be replaced by Betsy von Furstenberg. But when she heard the writers were thinking about killing off Lisa, she made another comeback. “I don't think anybody would believe Lisa is dead unless I do it,” she said. Fulton co-authored two autobiographies, 1970's How My World Turns and 1995's As My World Still Turns; several murder mysteries; and another book, 1999's Soap Opera: A Novel. She also was a cabaret performer and had her own clothing line at J.C. Penney. In real life, Fulton, unlike Lisa, was married (and divorced) only three times. Survivors include her brother, Charles, and her niece, Katherine. In a 2010 interview with NPR, the actress said she was well aware that many viewers despised her character. There was one in particular. “I was standing in front of Lord & Taylor. I'd only been on the show a few weeks,” she said. “And this beautifully dressed woman in a Chanel suit — in the days before there were knockoffs — came up to me and said, ‘Aren't you Lisa?' And I said, ‘Yes, that's the part I play.' And she said, ‘Well, I hate you!' And she hit me! And people looked at me like I was rotten and this woman was a heroine. “But I thought, ‘You know what? I've reached them.' Then a telegram came into the studio. It said, ‘If that bitch Lisa marries Bob I'll never watch As the World Turns again.' That is how the character was truly locked in.” Sign up for THR news straight to your inbox every day Send us a tip using our anonymous form.

The January-premiering third season of the show — about a group of friends in Charleston, S.C. working at Leva Bonaparte's crown jewel nightclub on King Street — saw Kulp face allegations of a cheating scandal with now-fiancée Emmy Sharrett. Source: Rolling Stone    Published: 2025-07-20 03:25:39

By Althea Legaspi WNBA All-Star players got straight to the point on the court ahead of their All-Star game on Saturday: “Pay Us What You Owe Us” their T-shirts read as they warmed up. The players union and league management have been in ongoing collective bargaining agreement negotiations. On Thursday, more than 40 players attended a Collective Bargaining Agreement (CBA) meeting, which apparently did not land on a mutually agreeable deal getting done. Indiana Fever star Caitlin Clark was at the meeting. “We should be paid more and hopefully that's the case moving forward as the league continues to grow,” Clark said in a video posted on social platform X. “I think that's something that's probably the most important thing that we're in the room advocating about.” Clark, who was present at the All-Star game on Saturday, was unable to play due to a right groin injury. Thursday's CBA meeting was the first time the league and the players union, the Women's National Basketball Players Association (WNBPA), have met in person since December. “We were disappointed for sure,” co-WNBA All-Star captain Napheesa Collier said on Friday, via ESPN. “What they came back with was just nowhere near what we asked for or even in the same conversation.” Ahead of the game, WNBA commissioner Cathy Engelbert offered an optimistic viewpoint contrasting the players' apparent outlook on the negotiations. “We want the same things that the players want,” Engelbert said in a Saturday press conference prior to game time, via Sportico. “We want to significantly increase their salary and benefits while balancing with our owners their ability to have a path to profitability as well as continued investment.” Trending Stories Belgium's Tomorrowland Saved by Metallica After Fire Destroys Main Stage Trump Asks Senate Leader to Cancel Summer Recess to Confirm His 'Incredible Nominees' Democrats Are Preparing a Deliberately Incomplete 2024 Election Autopsy Trump and the Catholic Church Fight a Law Requiring Clergy to Report Child Abuse The opposing viewpoints highlight how far apart the WNBPA and league management appear to be in negotiations. The labor fight is centered on the union's call for a revamp on revenue sharing, where players would receive a bigger percentage of league revenue. Englebert has said the next pass will be “much more lucrative.” However, players have said that what has been recently proposed was far from “equitable.” As the WNBA grapples with labor negotiations, it has also been expanding, with three new cities being added in the next five years. By Naomi LaChance President Donald Trump said Senate Majority Leader John Thune (R-S.D.) should cancel the Senate's summer break and long weekends in order to confirm Trump's nominees, which include some controversial picks, more quickly in a Truth Social post Saturday. “Hopefully the very talented John Thune, fresh off our many victories over the past two weeks and, indeed, 6 months, will cancel August recess (and long weekends!), in order to get my incredible nominees confirmed,” Trump wrote. “We need them badly!!!” The Senate is expected to go on recess from Aug. 4 to Sept. 1. It is one of 14 breaks or long weekends on the 2025 calendar. Their most recent break was June 30 to July 4, and then there is another break toward the end of September. Even when the Senate is in session, lawmakers are generally only in their Capitol Hill offices a few days a week, with ample time to travel back home. Senators are scheduled to vote on six nominations on Monday, including Bradley Hansell for under secretary of defense for intelligence and security, and John Hurley for under secretary for terrorism and financial crimes. The Senate is also slated for a major vote on a funding bill. Popular on Rolling Stone The Senate could soon vote on Emil Bove, a controversial nominee to become a judge on a federal appeals court. He served as one of Trump's personal lawyers before taking a role at the Justice Department. A whistleblower said in June that Bove told lawyers at the Justice Department they “would need to consider telling the courts ‘fuck you' and ignore any such court order” that would block Trump from sending immigrants to prison in El Salvador. The Senate Judiciary Committee advanced his nomination earlier this week, prompting Democrats to walk out. “I have respect for you Mr. Chairman, but this is outrageous, this is unacceptable, this is wrong,” said Sen. Cory Booker (D-N.J.). “This is an abuse of power. It is an undermining of the wellbeing and the integrity of this Senate.” Editor's picks The 100 Best TV Episodes of All Time The 250 Greatest Albums of the 21st Century So Far More than 75 former judges asked the Senate Judiciary Committee to reject Bove's nomination. “Mr. Bove's egregious record of mistreating law enforcement officers, abusing power, and disregarding the law itself disqualifies him for this position,” the group wrote. Dallas filmmaker takes on Trump shooting in shadow of JFK's assassination
Source: Spectrum News    Published: 2025-07-20 16:14:00

Get the best experience and stay connected to your community with our Spectrum News app. Learn More Get the best experience and stay connected to your community with our Spectrum News app. Learn More Continue in Browser Get hyperlocal forecasts, radar and weather alerts. Please enter a valid zipcode. Save DALLAS — One year after the assassination attempt on President Donald Trump, one of the first major films delving into conspiracy theories around the shooting will premiere; not far from the home of one of the nation's biggest conspiracy theories. The documentary “Who Shot Trump” is already streaming online and will have its theatrical premiere at the Angelika Film Center Dallas on Sunday, July 27. In the documentary, filmmaker J.D. Wilcox investigates the shooting that took place near Butler, Pennsylvania, on July 13, 2024, and tries to find answers about what all took place that day. Wilcox, who lives in the Dallas area, said he was instantly drawn to investigate the situation, as he watched the incident unfold live on TV that day. After all, given where he calls home these days, he said this isn't the first presidential shooting he's taken a closer look at. “For an investigative reporter, this is sort of like Mecca,” said Wilcox as he stood on the Grassy Knoll at Dallas' Dealey Plaza. “You have to come here.” Dealey Plaza is, of course, where President John F. Kennedy was assassinated on Nov. 22, 1963. In the 60-plus years since, some of the world's most prominent and well-known conspiracy theories have sprung up around the incident—hypotheses about additional shooters and government or organized crime involvements, just to name a few. Wilcox said he's done his fair share of investigation into that incident as well, but instantly shifted his focus to the Trump shooting last year. “There's absolutely been a cover-up,” said Wilcox. In the year since then-candidate Trump was shot at while on stage at a campaign rally, several investigations into the incident have taken place concluding various issues and errors occurred that day but ultimately that the blame for the shooting lies on 20-year-old Thomas Crooks, who was shot and killed by the Secret Service that day. Many continue to question the incident, including Wilcox. “My crew and I went to Butler, Pennsylvania,” he said with skilled investigators and experts, “and during that process, we uncovered really, really substantial forensic evidence.” Wilcox hopes his findings and thoughts on the incident will help lead to more clarity on that day, but as a North Texan, his thoughts go to that infamous conspiracy theory stemming from 1963 as well. As Wilcox stood at Dealey Plaza, dozens of visitors toured the historic site around him, many of whom openly presented their own theories to one another about “who really shot JFK” and “what really happened that day.” Reflecting on his new documentary and the many other conspiracy theories he's heard online and in the community about the Trump assassination attempt, Wilcox ponders if that incident will have a similar legacy to the Kennedy one, drawing visitors to theorize in Butler decades later. “My hope is that 60 years from now, we don't have the mystery that we have today,” said Wilcox. Whether viewers agree with his take or dismiss it, he hopes it'll keep the conversation going and keep encouraging others to ask questions about this new moment in presidential history, just like they still do with the 60-year-old one in Dallas.

Source: NDTV    Published: 2025-07-20 15:34:52

The Annabelle doll, a supposedly haunted relic, was found missing from paranormal investigator Dan Rivera's hotel room after his death in Gettysburg, Pennsylvania, People reported. The 54-year-old was found dead in his hotel room on July 13 after leading a sold-out ghost tour called "Devils on the Run" at the Soldiers National Orphanage, which featured the Annabelle doll. The cause of death remains unknown, with autopsy results expected in eight to ten weeks. However, the authorities confirmed that Rivera's death didn't appear suspicious, and he was found alone in his hotel room. Adams County Coroner Francis Dutrow told People Friday that the doll wasn't in the room when first responders found Rivera. Also Read | Jack Ma Spotted Riding Bicycle On Chinese Streets, Internet Says, "Simplicity At Its Peak" The Annabelle doll is believed to be haunted and has been linked to a series of paranormal activities since the 1970s. According to the New England Society for Psychic Research's website, the doll was gifted to a student nurse. She brought it home, where she lived with her roommate in 1968. "Almost immediately, the roommates noticed strange occurrences with the doll and they were introduced to a medium who told them the doll was inhabited by the spirit of a young girl named Annabelle," the organisation wrote. "The two roommates tried to accept the doll's spirit and please it only to have it reciprocate maliciousness and violent intent." Ed and Lorraine Warren, renowned paranormal investigators, claimed the doll was "demonically possessed". The doll also inspired the horror film franchise The Conjuring. Also Read | What Is Baby Grok? Musk's xAI Announces Kid-Friendly AI Chatbot After Companion Controversy Conspiracy theorists have linked Rivera's death to the Annabelle doll, despite police statements that nothing unusual or suspicious was found at the scene. Some fans and followers are also speculating about the doll's curse, while others are paying tribute to Rivera's work and legacy. In a report shared on July 16, the Pennsylvania State Police said, "Members from PSP Gettysburg responded to a hotel in Straban Township, Adams County for a report of a deceased [man]." "The decedent was discovered in his hotel room by workers. Nothing unusual or suspicious was observed at the scene." Despite Rivera's death, the New England Society for Psychic Research plans to continue their supernatural tour, honouring Rivera's memory. If You Miss Supernatural, The Perfect Replacement Is A Hit Sci-Fi Show That's Almost As Long
Source: Screen Rant    Published: 2025-07-20 12:25:00

If you're still missing Supernatural, you should check out this similar show that will give you plenty to binge watch. Following brothers Sam (Jared Padalecki) and Dean (Jensen Ackles) Winchester as they travel around the country hunting monsters, Supernatural ran for an impressive fifteen seasons on the CW. Supernatural brilliantly combined monster-of-the-week episodes with season-long storylines, developing a complex mythology throughout its fifteen seasons. There are a lot of shows out there with elements that could appeal to Supernatural fans, but perhaps no show feels as much like Supernatural as The X-Files. With its stories of cross-country monster hunting, Supernatural was heavily influenced by The X-Files, and even referenced the show in its pilot episode. The X-Files follows FBI Agents Fox Mulder (David Duchovny) and Dana Scully (Gillian Anderson) as they handle the cases that are too strange for the regular FBI. The best X-Files episodes include Monster of the Week and Alien mythology episodes, making it an iconic show. Where many of Supernatural's monsters come from folklore, The X-Files skews more paranormal, diving into conspiracy theories involving UFOs and alien abductions. Both shows blend horror, drama, and humor in fascinating ways, and both feature unforgettable characters you cannot help but fall in love with. Several actors have appeared in both shows, including Mark Sheppard and Mitch Pileggi. A few crew members worked on both shows as well, most notably Kim Manners, who served as both a director and producer. Several Supernatural episodes borrow ideas from episodes of The X-Files, from the more frightening stories like "Family Remains" (The X-Files: "Home") to the hilarious ones like "Mystery Spot" (The X-Files: "Monday"). Like Supernatural, The X-Files combines standalone mysteries with season-long arcs, developing its own (sometimes convoluted) mythology. Few shows run as long as Supernatural, and a sixteenth season remains a distinct possibility, but The X-Files has plenty of content to keep you busy in the meantime. The X-Files initially aired from 1993 to 2002, delivering nine seasons (and a movie) of alien shenanigans and a will-they-won't-they romance for the ages. The X-Files season 9 is the lowest-rated out of any season of the acclaimed science fiction series so what exactly went so wrong with it? The first X-Files movie, The X-Files: Fight the Future, premiered in theaters between seasons 5 and 6 and focused on the show's ongoing mythology. A second film, The X-Files: I Want to Believe, premiered in theaters in 2008, delivering a standalone story but ultimately ending the series on a lackluster note. Although X-Files creator Chris Carter had plans for a third film, I Want to Believe did not perform well enough at the box office to warrant a sequel. In 2016, Agents Mulder and Scully returned yet again for more alien adventures in a revival that lasted for two seasons on Fox network. While the mythology aspects of these seasons were met with mixed reviews, they nevertheless delivered some incredibly fun episodes that are well worth watching. Another X-Files reboot is currently in the works from Sinners director Ryan Coogler, proving that just like Supernatural, The X-Files refuses to stay dead for long. Bosch: Legacy's cancellation was a huge disappointment for viewers, but luckily, the character has already returned in the new spinoff show.

Paranormal investigation will raise money for Playcrafters Barn Theatre, Moline
Source: OurQuadCities    Published: 2025-07-20 12:00:00

WHBF - OurQuadCities.com Please enter a search term. Please enter a search term. by: Linda Cook Posted: Jul 20, 2025 / 07:00 AM CDT Updated: Jul 19, 2025 / 06:42 PM CDT by: Linda Cook Posted: Jul 20, 2025 / 07:00 AM CDT Updated: Jul 19, 2025 / 06:42 PM CDT On Sunday, July 27, from 7-9 p.m., you can take part in the first paranormal investigation at Playcrafters Barn Theatre in Moline, a news release says. QC Haunts & History, S&S Paranormal Investigations, and Haunted Maps will lead the investigations. Proceeds will go to directly to Playcrafters. The theater's history dates back to 1929 with a group of “wandering” actors and crew who performed anywhere they could. In 1958, Dr. William Otis gave Playcrafters the dairy barn from the Deere Experimental Farm. The barn was built in 1914. It had been sitting unused since 1933 on the Otis property. On Oct. 5, 1960, Playcrafters performed its first production, “Born Yesterday,” in its new home. “People hear footsteps going up and down the stairs. My husband and I have heard people talking on the stage when no one's there. We've checked around to find out who it was, but we haven't found anyone in those cases. It's just been us,” said Jacque Cohoon, Playcrafters board president. “We're very curious about what we'll find during the paranormal investigation.” The cost of the ghost hunt is $40 per person. Recommended age is 13 and up; children under 18 must be accompanied by an adult. To purchase tickets, contact Minda here or text 309-781-7083. Participants will have access to equipment and will be joined by experienced paranormal investigators. “While we enjoy guiding people during these events and discovering what we can about the history of the location and those who came before us, what's most important to us is to help local businesses—especially the arts. Whether you're a believer in the supernatural or not, I think we can all agree that supporting our community is important,” said Minda Powers-Douglas of QC Haunts & History. QC Haunts also offers ghost tours in downtown Rock Island and the Village of East Davenport. Visit here for more information. Copyright 2025 Nexstar Media Inc. All rights reserved. 10 Once-Great TV Shows That Lasted Way Too Long (& Went Downhill)
Source: Comic Book Resources    Published: 2025-07-20 01:00:00

Everyone always roots for their favorite TV series to enjoy long runs, but when they do, there's always a chance that they will go downhill. Such is the case with some of the most popular series of all time, like Dexter or The Simpsons. And while there are cases of shows recovering after going downhill, like The Simpsons, more commonly, a good show turned bad is likely to only get worse the longer it goes on. Far too often, the best TV shows will destroy their legacies by lasting far too long and failing to maintain their quality. They ruin their characters, confuse their lore, and pump out episodes endlessly without a point in sight. Not all of these series necessarily went on for a massively long time, but they all needed to end far sooner than they did. Supernatural has become the poster child for TV series that needed to die far sooner than they did. In its early years, the urban fantasy was a fun spiritual successor to Buffy the Vampire Slayer and Angel, depicting the episodic adventures of demon hunters Sam and Dean Winchester, while also building out its interesting lore and dramatic central conflict. While the series' premise was strong enough to work initially, it did not have nearly enough fuel to keep the show going for the 15 seasons that it ended up running for. Supernatural was originally intended to end with the conclusion of Season 5. For 10 seasons and over 200 episodes, Supernatural is an unbearable, repetitive slog. The longest-running series to never win an Emmy, not once during its latter two-thirds, did it ever come close to being worthy of one. Not every season of Supernatural post-Season 5 is outright terrible, with some even being okay, but they're bereft of original ideas, the poor treatment of the supporting cast becomes increasingly inexcusable, and the main cast becomes downright annoying to follow. Your comment has not been saved Nearly 20 years since it first premiered, How I Met Your Mother doesn't hold up at all, but there are still plenty of fun laughs and wholesome moments to be found in the traditional sitcom's early seasons. However, the core mystery of who Ted Mosby's future wife could be was not built to last for 9 seasons. As a result, the show becomes painfully boring and unfunny in its final seasons, and the series remains infamous for having one of the worst series finales of all time. The ending of How I Met Your Mother Season 9 was scripted during Season 1. How I Met Your Mother begins to get worse during Season 3, but it's Season 5 where it runs out of organic ideas and stops being funny. The switch in focus to Barney Stinson doesn't work at all, charming as Neil Patrick Harris may be, and all the time devoted to him and his romance with Robin Scherbatsky is rendered meaningless by Season 9. And, while its finale may overshadow everything else about it, Season 9 as a whole is still one of the weakest final seasons for any sitcom. Your comment has not been saved While Dexter initially got continually worse with each season after its first outing, it blew fans away with the unmatched brilliance of Season 4. The conflict between serial killer Dexter Morgan and the even more monstrous Trinity Killer made for some of the best TV drama of the 2000s, and it seemed impossible that the show would ever be able to top itself. Sure enough, this proved to be the case, although no one could have predicted what a roller coaster of quality Dexter's final four seasons would be. Since the airing of its finale, Dexter has received two sequel series, as well as a prequel series. From Game of Thrones to Breaking Bad to The Sopranos, some of the best TV shows to date are those with mature audiences in mind. Dexter Season 5 isn't bad, but it marks the biggest drop in quality in the series yet, and it kills all the momentum from Season 4. Season 6, meanwhile, is a boring, nonsensical mess that actively insults its audience's intelligence. Seasons 7 and 8 are better than Season 6, because they had to be, but still neither comes close to matching the quality of Dexter's earlier years. Your comment has not been saved Suits is a series about Mike Ross, a fake lawyer at a prestigious law firm who constantly works to make sure no one finds out he never actually went to law school. While not the series' only strong point, it was very much carried by the endlessly entertaining dynamic between Mike and his smarmy but charming mentor, Harvey Specter. Despite it being well-known that this was the main draw of the show, Suits continued on even after Mike left the series. Both of Suits' spin-off series, Pearson and Suits L.A., were canceled after only a single season. Throughout its first five seasons, Suits burns through its premise as every major character learns Mike's secret one-by-one, before he's openly exposed as a fraud. The end of Season 5 is the series' high point, and Season 6 could have made for an effective epilogue, as it shows what Mike does next after losing everything. Instead, Suits trucked on for three more years, with Season 7 being underwhelming, Season 8 being a complete disaster due to Mike's total absence from it, and Season 9 only being marginally better, even with Mike's return. Your comment has not been saved Killing Eve may have only lasted four seasons, but the damage done by its final season is still worse than nearly any other in television history. For its first three seasons, its quality wasn't exactly consistent, but the series never came close to being bad, and the steamy drama between MI5 agent Eve Polastri and professional assassin Villanelle. Regardless of Season 3's many flaws, the two leads remained immensely deep and compelling, and there remained a strong desire among fans to receive pay-off for all the romantic and sexual tension between them. Season 4 of Killing Eve is the only season with a rotten rating on Rotten Tomatoes. Season 4 is so horrendously offensive that it defeats the point of even bothering with the first three seasons. What was previously hailed as one of the best LGBTQ+ dramas on television turns actively homophobic, leading to one of the worst endings in TV history. It's hard to say when Killing Eve should have ended, but Season 4 never should have been allowed to exist. Your comment has not been saved The first season of Elite is nothing short of iconic. Every member of the ensemble cast is well-developed, every episode is filled with memorable scenes, and the core mystery surrounding the murder of Marina Nunier is flawlessly constructed. Seasons 2 and 3 failed to be quite as legendary, but were still exceptional. The same cannot be said for the subsequent five seasons. Along with its eight seasons, seven special Elite "Shorts" were released. With so many streaming services for viewers to binge-watch TV shows like Game of Thrones and Breaking Bad, the choices can be overwhelming. With a change of writers and the loss of most of its best characters, Elite loses everything that made it great, beginning with Season 4. The show turns its focus away from interesting stories in favor of finding ways to include as many sex scenes as possible, and the stories it does tell range from boring to offensive. Season 8 is decent, but it is absolutely not worth sitting through Seasons 4-7 in order to get there. Your comment has not been saved You's first season was a competent thriller, but not one anyone would expect to lead to four more seasons, with it largely being carried by Penn Badgley's brilliant performance as the enigmatic and despicable Joe Goldberg. Season 2 is where the series became something truly special, thanks to its subversion of Season 1's formula and the introduction of the show's best character, Love Quinn. After peaking, however, You just continued to get worse with each of its following three seasons. You began life as a Lifetime series, before finding a permanent home on Netflix, beginning with Season 2. Season 3 is where Joe becomes insufferable, not just as a person, but as a protagonist, and the plot is the least interesting yet. Seasons 4 and 5, meanwhile, are complete nonsense that lack any of the atmosphere or effective twists of Seasons 1 and 2, and that lose track of who Joe is as a character. By the time Season 5 ends, Badgley's acting is far from enough to make the show bearable. Your comment has not been saved With its first two parts, Money Heist tells a fantastic, complete story that's enjoyable from start to finish and that does justice to all its main characters. The show was about a group of masters in their field coming together to perform the ultimate robbery, as they grow as individuals and together as a found family, and it executed this premise to near perfection. But, due to Money Heist's popularity, it received an additional three parts that ruined the flawless ending of the first two. Money Heist received a Korean remake in 2022. The final three parts of Money Heist ask, "what if everything that went right from the robbers during the first heist went wrong?" and the result is genuinely compelling drama, with some great new characters being added to the mix as well. The problem is that they pointlessly rip away the happy endings of several fan-favorite characters, killing several of them off in cruel, borderline sexist ways, and it does this while feeling like it lacks any real point. Every season of Money Heist is perfectly watchable, but its latter three are noticeably weaker, and they retroactively make the first two parts worse. Your comment has not been saved No series with so much initial promise has ever wound up being as bad as Sliders. For its first two seasons, Sliders is an inconsistent series, but one with a lot of heart and passion behind it, that chronicles the adventures of a genius college student, his best friend, his professor, and a washed-up musician as they travel between different versions of Earth, where history played out differently, in an effort to get back to their own home. At its best, Sliders offers some of the greatest sci-fi stories of its era, but from Season 3 onwards, episodes of that level become few and far between. Sliders was canceled by Fox after Season 3, but survived by moving to the Sci-Fi Channel. From Scrubs to Futurama and everything in between, some TV show episodes have ripped audiences' heartstrings out. Season 3 spends most of its time ripping off horror movies, and it marks the first of several instances of the series writing out its original cast members in horrible ways. Season 4 gets even worse, as the lore of the series is rewritten, and Sliders devolves into a generic and horribly executed sci-fi action series. By comparison, Season 5 is a bit better, but even it is mostly just boring, with each passing episode making a viewer question what they're even still doing here. Your comment has not been saved Gossip Girl Season 1 is one of the best and most influential seasons of television of the 21st Century. Depicting the scandalous lives of Manhattan's elite, it was bold, controversial, witty, steamy, fun and, perhaps most importantly, satirical. The tragic downward spiral Gossip Girl goes on throughout its six-season run can almost entirely be attributed to it forgetting that it was mocking the millionaires and billionaires it focuses on, not taking them, their meaningless drama, and their ridiculous schemes seriously. A Gossip Girl reboot was released on HBO Max in 2021 and ran for two seasons. While there is fun to be had with the middle seasons of Gossip Girl, the lack of bite and self-awareness hurts the series immensely. And the longer it goes on, the less fun it gets, especially as the focus increasingly gets placed on Chuck Bass. Gossip Girl doesn't even manage to stick the landing when it comes to the mystery surrounding the identity of its eponymous blogger, with the answer being one of the few people it literally could not have been.
